{"nick":"joepie91","message":"dshulgin2: I don't know of any resources I recommend that aren't really poor, but tl;dr: 1) don't try to make things look aesthetically nice; readability/maintainability are much more important, and sometimes the good-looking thing isn't the same as the readable thing, 2) don't try to make code \"perfectly consistent\" - often consistency contributes to readability, but not always, 3) don't try to make code shorter, often more verbose code is clearer,","date":"2017-02-16T11:17:48.298Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"4) don't abbreviate variable names; if a variable name is too long, remove words, not letters, 5) modularize everything into loosely coupled bits, 6) avoid mutation where you can, 7) never use global state, implicit dependencies, or other non-obvious shared state","date":"2017-02-16T11:17:49.786Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"(re: loose coupling: https://gist.github.com/joepie91/7f03a733a3a72d2396d6 )","date":"2017-02-16T11:18:00.180Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"rchavik","date":"2017-02-16T11:18:03.407Z","type":"join"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"8) use promises instead of error-first callbacks, consistently, 9) don't be afraid to rewrite or redesign a chunk of code if it's unclear in its current state, 10) never add comments that explain *what* the code does, because this should be obvious from the code itself (and you should improve the code until it is); rather, comments should tell you *why* the code does what it does, when it isn't obvious","date":"2017-02-16T11:19:13.398Z","type":"message"}
